# Minimal launch subset

If the requirement is not “everything eventually needed” but “minimum for a strong foundation,” then the true minimum launch package is this subset:

| Required minimum | Why |
| --- | --- |
| Vision and scope charter | Prevents conceptual drift |
| V1 architecture specification | Core design anchor |
| Ontology and relation catalog | Defines the substrate |
| `Atom`, `TextAtom`, `CodeAtom`, source, provenance, recipe schemas | Core data model |
| Text refinery spec | First ingestion path |
| Code refinery spec | Technical ingestion path |
| CAS model and raw archive policy | Exact state plus audit |
| Graph and vector indexing strategy | Retrieval backbone |
| GraphQL schema | Unified access surface |
| Validation and supersession policy | Trust and lifecycle control |
| Retrieval and assembly spec | Makes the system useful |
| Pilot SOP and QA rubric | Makes the system operable |
| Benchmark corpus and readiness scorecard | Makes the launch measurable |

* * *

# Final recommendation

For first construction, treat the launch package in three rings.

**Ring 1** is mandatory foundation: architecture, ontology, schemas, storage decisions, refinery specs, retrieval model, governance rules.

**Ring 2** is operational hardening: SOPs, QA harnesses, dashboards, benchmarks, release checklists.

**Ring 3** is expansion: richer templates, broader runtime support, live editor integration, automated remediation loops.

The correct next move is to turn this into a **document-grade v1 spec package** with section numbering, normative language (`MUST`, `SHOULD`, `MAY`), and appendices for schemas and artifact manifests.

## Q: 
Proceed

## A: 
# Unified Atomic Knowledge Substrate v1

## Document-Grade Architecture Specification Package

**Document ID:** `uaks_v1_architecture_spec_20260311`  
**Version:** `1.0-draft`  
**Status:** Draft for foundational launch  
**Normative language:** The key words **MUST**, **MUST NOT**, **SHOULD**, **SHOULD NOT**, and **MAY** are to be interpreted as requirement levels.

* * *

## 0. Front Matter

### 0.1 Purpose

This document defines the v1 architecture for a unified atomic substrate that treats textual knowledge and technical logic as first-class, governed, addressable units. It establishes the normative requirements for ontology, schemas, storage, refinement, retrieval, assembly, governance, interfaces, and foundational launch artifacts.

### 0.2 Scope

This specification covers:

| Area | Included |
| --- | --- |
| Atom model | Yes |
| Text atoms | Yes |
| Code atoms | Yes |
| Graph relations | Yes |
| Provenance | Yes |
| CAS | Yes |
| Raw source archive | Yes |
| Vector retrieval | Yes |
| GraphQL interface | Yes |
| Governance | Yes |
| Launch artifact inventory | Yes |

This specification does not attempt to standardize distributed peer-to-peer replication, autonomous code rewriting, or universal language support in v1.

### 0.3 System designation

| Field | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Canonical name | Unified Atomic Knowledge Substrate |
| Abbreviation | UAKS |
| Version | v1 |
| System type | Hybrid semantic-graph, content-addressed, provenance-governed assembly substrate |

* * *

## 1. Executive Thesis

UAKS-v1 is a substrate, not a folder tree, not a document library, and not merely a chatbot memory layer.

The substrate MUST store persistent knowledge as atomic units.  
It MUST store logical structure as explicit relations.  
It MUST store exact state as immutable content-addressed objects.  
It MUST preserve raw source artifacts for audit and re-refinement.  
It MUST generate human-facing artifacts as assembled outputs or saved recipes rather than treat static documents as the primary truth objects.

The system’s central design claim is:

**Text and code belong to one ontology but require different refinery disciplines.**

* * *

## 2. Governing Principles

| Principle ID | Principle | Normative statement |
| --- | --- | --- |
| GP-01 | Atom-first persistence | The system MUST treat atoms as the primary active knowledge substrate. |
| GP-02 | Hybrid retrieval | The system MUST combine graph and vector retrieval with governance and temporal constraints. |
| GP-03 | Provenance integrity | Every verified atom MUST retain a precise provenance chain. |
| GP-04 | Immutable content state | Content-addressed payloads MUST be immutable. |
| GP-05 | Logical supersession | Conceptual continuity MUST be represented via explicit supersession relations rather than silent overwrite. |
| GP-06 | Cross-domain traceability | Business or policy text SHOULD be linkable to implementing or affected code. |
| GP-07 | Assembly over static document | Output documents SHOULD be reproducible from recipes and atoms. |
| GP-08 | Resolution elasticity | The same substrate MUST support multiple output scales. |
| GP-09 | Specialized refinement | Text and code MUST have distinct refinement pipelines under one governance model. |
| GP-10 | Auditability | The system MUST support inspection of source, transformation, and assembly lineage. |

* * *

## 3. Core Requirements

### 3.1 Functional requirements

| ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| FR-01 | The system MUST ingest raw text, conversational text, code, scripts, config, and rich source artifacts. |
| FR-02 | The system MUST produce `TextAtom` and `CodeAtom` as first-class outputs of refinery pipelines. |
| FR-03 | The system MUST assign stable logical identifiers to atoms. |
| FR-04 | The system MUST assign content hashes to immutable payload states. |
| FR-05 | The system MUST preserve original raw sources in an archive. |
| FR-06 | The system MUST support graph relations among atoms and entities. |
| FR-07 | The system MUST support semantic retrieval via vector indexing where applicable. |
| FR-08 | The system MUST support typed query access through a unified interface. |
| FR-09 | The system MUST support recipe-based assembly of outputs. |
| FR-10 | The system MUST support supersession, contradiction marking, and validation state transitions. |

### 3.2 Nonfunctional requirements

| ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| NFR-01 | Verified atoms MUST have complete provenance. |
| NFR-02 | Hashing MUST be deterministic for equivalent canonical payloads. |
| NFR-03 | Retrieval MUST permit hybrid scoring across graph, vector, temporal, and governance dimensions. |
| NFR-04 | Exact content states MUST be reconstructable from CAS references. |
| NFR-05 | Re-refinement MUST be possible from raw archived sources. |
| NFR-06 | The system SHOULD tolerate partial refinement failure without global data loss. |
| NFR-07 | The system SHOULD support incremental update processing. |
| NFR-08 | The system MUST preserve traceability across text-to-code bridges where established. |

* * *

## 4. Logical System Topology

### 4.1 Core layers

| Layer | Mandatory | Role |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Source Intake Layer | Yes | Registers and fingerprints incoming sources |
| Raw Source Archive | Yes | Stores original source artifacts intact |
| Text Refinery | Yes | Produces text atoms from human-language sources |
| Code Refinery | Yes | Produces code atoms from technical sources |
| Graph Layer | Yes | Stores explicit relations and dependency structure |
| Vector Layer | Yes | Stores embeddings for semantic retrieval |
| CAS Layer | Yes | Stores immutable content-addressed payloads |
| Metadata / Governance Layer | Yes | Tracks states, review events, lineage, and policy |
| Assembly Layer | Yes | Builds outputs from selected atoms |
| Interface Layer | Yes | Exposes typed query and control surface |

### 4.2 Trust boundaries

| Boundary | Authoritative source |
| --- | --- |
| Raw source truth | Raw Source Archive |
| Exact payload state | CAS |
| Conceptual continuity | Atom logical ID and supersession chain |
| Explicit relational truth | Graph Layer |
| Semantic neighborhood | Vector Layer |
| Human-facing assembled output | Assembly Layer, bounded by source-backed atoms |

* * *

## 5. Ontology Overview

### 5.1 Root object families

| Family | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Atom | Abstract base type for all atomic units |
| TextAtom | Atomic textual meaning unit |
| CodeAtom | Atomic executable or technical logic unit |
| Entity | Domain object referenced by atoms |
| Relation | Typed connection between atoms or between atoms and entities |
| SourceObject | Registered raw source artifact |
| ProvenanceRecord | Transformation and lineage object |
| Recipe | Persisted assembly plan |
| ValidationEvent | Review or state-transition record |

### 5.2 First-class mandate

`TextAtom` and `CodeAtom` MUST be modeled as peer first-class types.  
Neither MUST be modeled as a lower-trust annotation on the other.  
Both MUST inherit from `Atom`.

* * *

## 6. Abstract Atom Specification

### 6.1 Base schema

| Field | Type | Required | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `atomId` | ULID or UUID | Yes | Stable logical identity |
| `atomType` | Enum | Yes | `TEXT` or `CODE` |
| `atomClass` | Enum | Yes | Functional role |
| `contentHash` | Hash | Yes | Immutable payload identity |
| `canonicalPayloadRef` | CASRef | Yes | Pointer to exact payload in CAS |
| `sourceRef` | ID | Yes | Originating source object |
| `provenanceRef` | ID | Yes | Latest provenance record |
| `validationState` | Enum | Yes | Lifecycle state |
| `confidenceScore` | Float | Yes | Confidence of correctness or extraction integrity |
| `taxonomyTags` | Array<String> | Yes | Domain and role tags |
| `scopeTags` | Array<String> | No | Project, audience, jurisdiction, domain scope |
| `effectiveFrom` | Timestamp | No | Start of validity |
| `effectiveTo` | Timestamp | No | End of validity |
| `supersedes` | Atom ID | No | Previous logical state |
| `supersededBy` | Atom ID | No | Later logical state |
| `createdAt` | Timestamp | Yes | Creation time |
| `updatedAt` | Timestamp | Yes | Metadata update time |
| `status` | Enum | Yes | Active, archived, hidden, blocked |

### 6.2 Base atom classes

| `atomClass` value | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `AXIOM` | Foundational invariant or principle |
| `FACT` | Verifiable declarative statement |
| `RULE` | Business, legal, policy, or system rule |
| `PROCEDURE` | Ordered operational instruction |
| `EVIDENCE` | Source-backed support unit |
| `INTERPRETATION` | Explicit inference or synthesis |
| `INTERFACE` | Input-output or contract definition |
| `DEPENDENCY` | Structural dependency expression |
| `TEST` | Assertion or executable validation |
| `RECIPE` | Saved assembly plan as an atomized object if needed |

### 6.3 Atom invariants

| Invariant ID | Invariant |
| --- | --- |
| AI-01 | Every atom MUST have one logical ID and one content hash. |
| AI-02 | Every verified atom MUST resolve to an archived source or a derivation chain terminating in archived sources. |
| AI-03 | Every atom MUST have an explicit type and class. |
| AI-04 | Verified atoms MUST NOT be silently overwritten. |
| AI-05 | Atoms SHOULD be independently interpretable within their subtype rules. |

* * *

## 7. TextAtom Specification

### 7.1 Definition

A `TextAtom` is the smallest self-contained textual unit that expresses a coherent meaning, claim, rule, instruction, evidence fragment, or interpretation without depending on hidden neighboring prose for basic comprehension.

### 7.2 TextAtom schema

| Field | Type | Required | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `textKind` | Enum | Yes | Note, requirement, policy, transcript-claim, documentation-clause, evidence-fragment |
| `canonicalStatement` | Text | Yes | Self-contained textual statement |
| `sourceSpan` | Span | Yes | Exact source location |
| `entitiesMentioned` | Array<ID> | Yes | Referenced entities |
| `claimPolarity` | Enum | No | Positive, negative, conditional, comparative |
| `temporalTag` | Enum | No | Current, historical, projected, obsolete |
| `evidenceRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Supporting evidence links |
| `contradictionRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Conflicting claims |
| `parentTextAtomRefs` | Array<ID> | No | More abstract atoms |
| `childTextAtomRefs` | Array<ID> | No | More granular atoms |

### 7.3 TextAtom acceptance rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| TA-01 | The `canonicalStatement` MUST be understandable without hidden local context. |
| TA-02 | The atom MUST have exact source span provenance. |
| TA-03 | Key referents MUST be explicit or resolvable through linked entities. |
| TA-04 | Rules, requirements, and policies SHOULD carry scope or temporal qualifiers when necessary. |
| TA-05 | Interpretive atoms MUST be marked as interpretation rather than fact. |

* * *

## 8. CodeAtom Specification

### 8.1 Definition

A `CodeAtom` is the smallest operationally meaningful technical unit suitable for dependency reasoning, traceability, impact analysis, and state reconstruction.

A `CodeAtom` MUST NOT be restricted to “pure function” only. The v1 system MUST support multiple code atom categories.

### 8.2 CodeAtom categories

| Category | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `FUNCTION` | Standalone callable unit |
| `METHOD` | Callable bound to type/object context |
| `CLASS` | Type container or behavior container |
| `MODULE` | File or package-level semantic unit |
| `CONFIG` | Structured configuration definition |
| `QUERY` | Database or data-access primitive |
| `SCRIPT_STEP` | Shell or workflow step |
| `TEST_CASE` | Executable validation unit |
| `SCHEMA_UNIT` | Schema, migration, type model, interface model |
| `UI_COMPONENT` | Reusable user interface unit |
| `INFRA_UNIT` | Deployment or infrastructure logic unit |

### 8.3 CodeAtom schema

| Field | Type | Required | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `codeKind` | Enum | Yes | Code category |
| `language` | String | Yes | Source language |
| `runtime` | String | No | Execution/runtime environment |
| `signature` | JSON/Text | No | Inputs, outputs, modifiers, generics |
| `astNodeType` | String | Yes | Canonical AST classification |
| `symbolName` | String | No | Named symbol |
| `modulePath` | String | Yes | Logical projected workspace path |
| `astSpan` | Span | Yes | Exact location in source |
| `dependencyRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Direct dependencies |
| `dependentRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Reverse dependencies |
| `sideEffectProfile` | Enum | No | Pure, read-only, write, network, filesystem, external |
| `complexityScore` | Float | No | Static complexity estimate |
| `testRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Linked tests |
| `buildRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Linked build outputs or compiled objects |
| `businessRuleRefs` | Array<ID> | No | Linked policy or rule text atoms |
| `interfaceContractRef` | ID | No | Contract object |
| `breakingChangeRisk` | Enum | No | Low, medium, high |
| `contentAddressRef` | CASRef | Yes | Exact immutable payload pointer |

### 8.4 CodeAtom acceptance rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| CA-01 | A `CodeAtom` MUST map to a structurally valid span resolved by the code refinery. |
| CA-02 | A `CodeAtom` MUST record exact source location. |
| CA-03 | A `CodeAtom` MUST record language and AST node type. |
| CA-04 | If dependencies are resolvable, they SHOULD be materialized as graph relations. |
| CA-05 | If a code unit enforces a policy or requirement, the system SHOULD permit a trace link to a `TextAtom`. |
| CA-06 | Content changes MUST yield a new content hash. |

* * *

## 9. Entity and Relation Model

### 9.1 Entity definition

An `Entity` is a named or canonicalized domain object referenced by atoms. Examples include business concepts, technical services, database tables, interfaces, policies, users, modules, runtime environments, and external systems.

### 9.2 Entity schema

| Field | Type | Required |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `entityId` | ID | Yes |
| `entityType` | String | Yes |
| `canonicalName` | String | Yes |
| `aliases` | Array<String> | No |
| `description` | Text | No |
| `status` | Enum | Yes |
| `createdAt` | Timestamp | Yes |

### 9.3 Relation types

| Relation | Source | Target | Meaning |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `IMPLEMENTS` | CodeAtom | TextAtom | Code enforces or realizes text rule |
| `DOCUMENTS` | TextAtom | CodeAtom | Text describes code |
| `DEPENDS_ON` | CodeAtom | CodeAtom | Technical dependency |
| `TESTS` | CodeAtom or TestAtom | CodeAtom | Validation relationship |
| `USES_ENTITY` | Atom | Entity | References domain object |
| `SUPPORTED_BY` | TextAtom | TextAtom or Evidence | Evidence support |
| `CONTRADICTS` | Atom | Atom | Competing states or claims |
| `SUPERSEDES` | Atom | Atom | Logical successor |
| `DERIVED_FROM` | Atom | SourceObject | Origin linkage |
| `ASSEMBLED_IN` | Atom | Recipe | Used in recipe |
| `AFFECTS` | TextAtom | CodeAtom | Policy or requirement impacts code |
| `EXPOSES_INTERFACE` | CodeAtom | Entity or Contract | Interface definition linkage |

### 9.4 Relation invariants

| ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| RI-01 | Verified relations MUST resolve to existing node identities. |
| RI-02 | `SUPERSEDES` relations MUST NOT form cycles in normal use. |
| RI-03 | `DEPENDS_ON` SHOULD be directional. |
| RI-04 | `IMPLEMENTS` and `AFFECTS` SHOULD be available for traceability use cases. |

* * *

## 10. Source Intake and Raw Archive

### 10.1 Source intake requirement

Every inbound artifact MUST be registered as a `SourceObject` before refinement.

### 10.2 SourceObject schema

| Field | Type | Required |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `sourceId` | ID | Yes |
| `sourceType` | Enum | Yes |
| `origin` | String | Yes |
| `ingestedAt` | Timestamp | Yes |
| `checksum` | Hash | Yes |
| `mimeType` | String | Yes |
| `authorRef` | ID | No |
| `rightsClass` | Enum | No |
| `rawArchiveRef` | ID | Yes |

### 10.3 Archive rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| SA-01 | The raw archive MUST preserve original source material in an untouched form. |
| SA-02 | Archived objects MUST be referenced by stable archive identifiers. |
| SA-03 | Refinery outputs MUST remain traceable back to archived source objects. |
| SA-04 | Re-refinement MUST be possible from archived sources. |

* * *

## 11. Content-Addressable Storage

### 11.1 CAS function

The CAS layer stores immutable payload objects addressed by content hash rather than human file path.

### 11.2 CAS rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| CAS-01 | CAS objects MUST be immutable. |
| CAS-02 | Identical canonical payloads MUST produce the same content hash under the selected hashing standard. |
| CAS-03 | Any content mutation MUST produce a new content object and new hash. |
| CAS-04 | Atoms MUST reference exact CAS payloads for reproducibility. |
| CAS-05 | Human-facing stable names MAY exist as projection-layer constructs, but MUST NOT replace content identity. |

### 11.3 CAS object schema

| Field | Type | Required |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `casRef` | ID | Yes |
| `contentHash` | Hash | Yes |
| `contentType` | String | Yes |
| `canonicalizationVersion` | String | Yes |
| `byteSize` | Integer | Yes |
| `createdAt` | Timestamp | Yes |
| `storageLocation` | String | Yes |

* * *

## 12. Refinery Architecture

### 12.1 Shared refinery principle

Text and code MUST use separate refinement pipelines. They MUST share governance, provenance, identity, and publication rules.

* * *

## 13. Text Refinery Specification

### 13.1 Pipeline stages

| Stage | Description |
| --- | --- |
| TR-1 Segmentation | Split source based on structure and semantic cues |
| TR-2 Extraction | Identify entities, claims, temporal markers, evidence fragments |
| TR-3 Distillation | Rewrite into smallest independent units of value |
| TR-4 Typing | Assign text kind and atom class |
| TR-5 Linking | Connect evidence, parent-child structure, contradictions, entities |
| TR-6 Validation | Check atomicity, provenance, and clarity |
| TR-7 Publication | Persist payload, graph relations, metadata, and state |

### 13.2 Text refinery rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| TRR-01 | Distilled textual units MUST preserve source-backed meaning. |
| TRR-02 | Text atoms MUST carry exact source spans. |
| TRR-03 | Interpretive compression SHOULD be marked explicitly where inference occurs. |
| TRR-04 | Deduplication SHOULD merge equivalent claims while preserving provenance multiplicity. |

* * *

## 14. Code Refinery Specification

### 14.1 Pipeline stages

| Stage | Description |
| --- | --- |
| CR-1 Parse | Build AST or equivalent structural model |
| CR-2 Symbol extraction | Identify functions, methods, classes, configs, tests, modules |
| CR-3 Boundary determination | Decide code atom spans |
| CR-4 Dependency analysis | Resolve calls, imports, interfaces, bindings where possible |
| CR-5 Technical typing | Assign code kind, runtime, side-effect profile |
| CR-6 Bridge linking | Link code to tests, docs, rules, schemas, interfaces |
| CR-7 Validation | Verify parse validity, span integrity, content identity |
| CR-8 Publication | Persist payload, relations, metadata, and state |

### 14.2 Code refinery rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| CRR-01 | Code atomization MUST be structurally grounded, not solely text-chunk based. |
| CRR-02 | The code refinery SHOULD use AST-aware parsing for supported languages. |
| CRR-03 | Dependency edges SHOULD be recorded when robustly resolvable. |
| CRR-04 | The system MUST support reprocessing when parser capabilities improve. |
| CRR-05 | Tests, configs, schemas, and infrastructure logic MAY be emitted as `CodeAtom`s. |

* * *

## 15. Provenance Model

### 15.1 Provenance layers

| Layer | Description |
| --- | --- |
| Source provenance | Where the atom originated |
| Transformation provenance | How the atom was extracted, rewritten, merged, or validated |
| Assembly provenance | Which outputs and recipes used the atom |

### 15.2 ProvenanceRecord schema

| Field | Type | Required |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `provenanceId` | ID | Yes |
| `sourceRef` | ID | Yes |
| `operationType` | Enum | Yes |
| `inputRefs` | Array<ID> | Yes |
| `outputRefs` | Array<ID> | Yes |
| `operatorRef` | ID | No |
| `toolVersion` | String | No |
| `timestamp` | Timestamp | Yes |
| `notes` | Text | No |

### 15.3 Provenance rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| PR-01 | Every verified atom MUST have a provenance chain. |
| PR-02 | Merge and deduplication events MUST preserve all underlying source references. |
| PR-03 | Assemblies SHOULD be able to expose provenance for included atoms. |

* * *

## 16. Validation and Governance

### 16.1 Validation states

| State | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| `DRAFT` | Newly created, not yet conformance checked |
| `DISTILLED` | Machine-created and schema-valid |
| `REVIEWED` | Human or trusted review completed |
| `VERIFIED` | Approved for production assembly use |
| `DEPRECATED` | Retained but not normally active |
| `DISPUTED` | Truth or integrity challenged |

### 16.2 ValidationEvent schema

| Field | Type | Required |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `validationEventId` | ID | Yes |
| `targetRef` | ID | Yes |
| `previousState` | Enum | Yes |
| `newState` | Enum | Yes |
| `actorRef` | ID | No |
| `timestamp` | Timestamp | Yes |
| `reason` | Text | No |

### 16.3 Governance rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| GOV-01 | Verified atoms MUST NOT be overwritten in place. |
| GOV-02 | State transitions MUST be auditable. |
| GOV-03 | Contradictory atoms MAY coexist if clearly marked and scoped. |
| GOV-04 | High-risk rule-linked code SHOULD require review prior to verified status. |
| GOV-05 | Policy, legal, or requirement text SHOULD require review before verified use. |

* * *

## 17. Retrieval Architecture

### 17.1 Retrieval principle

Retrieval MUST be hybrid. No single substrate is sufficient for the required system behavior.

### 17.2 Retrieval score model

A generic retrieval score MAY be represented as:

$$
R(a, q) = w_sS(a,q) + w_gG(a,q) + w_tT(a,q) + w_vV(a) + w_uU(a) + w_cC(a) - w_dD(a,q)
$$

Where semantic similarity, graph relevance, temporal fit, validation trust, utility, and centrality are combined with penalties for distance, contradiction, or staleness.

### 17.3 Retrieval rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| RET-01 | Queries MUST be able to combine graph and vector criteria. |
| RET-02 | Validation state SHOULD affect ranking. |
| RET-03 | Temporal validity SHOULD affect ranking where time matters. |
| RET-04 | Code retrieval SHOULD weight dependency and symbol relations more heavily than prose-only similarity. |
| RET-05 | Text retrieval SHOULD weight evidence and scope coherence strongly. |

* * *

## 18. Resolution and Assembly

### 18.1 Resolution levels

| Level | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `MICRO` | Minimal core claim or logic path |
| `COMPACT` | Essential support only |
| `STANDARD` | Balanced explanatory output |
| `EXTENDED` | Detailed exposition or technical walkthrough |
| `DEEP` | Evidence-rich, edge-case inclusive, contradiction-aware output |

### 18.2 Recipe schema

| Field | Type | Required |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `recipeId` | ID | Yes |
| `recipeType` | Enum | Yes |
| `atomSequence` | Array<ID> | Yes |
| `templateRef` | ID | Yes |
| `resolutionLevel` | Enum | Yes |
| `generationRules` | JSON | No |
| `createdAt` | Timestamp | Yes |

### 18.3 Assembly rules

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| ASM-01 | Assembled outputs SHOULD be reproducible from saved recipes. |
| ASM-02 | The assembly layer MUST NOT fabricate unsupported factual content as if it were atom-backed truth. |
| ASM-03 | Connective prose MAY be generated to improve readability. |
| ASM-04 | Provenance exposure SHOULD be available for high-trust outputs. |

* * *

## 19. GraphQL Interface Specification

### 19.1 Interface role

The GraphQL layer is the typed access surface over graph, vector, CAS, archive, and governance services.

### 19.2 GraphQL principles

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| GQL-01 | The interface MUST expose `Atom`, `TextAtom`, `CodeAtom`, `Entity`, `SourceObject`, `ProvenanceRecord`, and `Recipe` types or equivalent queryable structures. |
| GQL-02 | Clients SHOULD be able to request only needed fields. |
| GQL-03 | Resolvers MUST enforce access and validation rules. |
| GQL-04 | The GraphQL layer MUST NOT be treated as the source of truth itself; it is a contract surface. |

### 19.3 Example query families

| Query family | Purpose |
| --- | --- |
| `atom(id)` | Retrieve a specific atom |
| `atoms(filter)` | Search and filter atom sets |
| `traceRuleToCode(ruleId)` | Find linked implementation code |
| `impactAnalysis(codeAtomId)` | Return affected dependents and linked rules/docs |
| `assemble(recipeId or querySpec)` | Produce output from atoms and template |
| `source(id)` | Retrieve source metadata |
| `provenance(id)` | Inspect lineage |

* * *

## 20. Decision Matrix

## Graph + Vector + CAS + Raw Source Archive + GraphQL API

### 20.1 Decision summary

| Component | v1 decision | Reason |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Graph | Mandatory | Explicit structure, dependencies, traceability |
| Vector | Mandatory | Semantic retrieval and approximate recall |
| CAS | Mandatory | Immutable state, deduplication, exact reconstruction |
| Raw Source Archive | Mandatory | Audit, provenance, re-refinement |
| GraphQL API | Mandatory for v1 contract | Typed unified access layer |

### 20.2 Benefit-cost-risk matrix

| Component | Benefits | Costs | Risk if absent |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Graph | Strong traceability, dependency reasoning, contradiction visibility | Ontology design overhead, edge management complexity | System collapses into loosely related chunks |
| Vector | Semantic recall, paraphrase matching, discovery | Embedding cost, refresh complexity, drift handling | Retrieval becomes brittle and keyword-bound |
| CAS | Immutable exact states, deduplication, snapshot reproducibility | Hash and object management complexity | No deterministic content state or exact replay |
| Raw Source Archive | Audit anchor, re-refinement, source recovery | Storage growth, archival discipline | Provenance breaks; future refinery upgrades blocked |
| GraphQL API | Unified typed interface, client flexibility, clean contract | Resolver complexity, schema governance | Fragmented interfaces, inconsistent access semantics |

### 20.3 Final judgment

All five components MUST be present in v1 if the system is intended as a serious foundational launch rather than a loose prototype.

* * *

## 21. Failure Modes and Countermeasures

| Failure mode | Description | Countermeasure |
| --- | --- | --- |
| False atomicity | Units too small or contextless | Enforce acceptance tests and parent-child relations |
| Semantic drift | Similar but wrong retrieval | Hybrid retrieval with graph and validation weighting |
| Provenance erosion | Atoms lose exact source trace | Mandatory provenance rules |
| Redundancy bloom | Near-duplicates multiply | Merge policy plus provenance-preserving deduplication |
| Stale recall | Old atoms dominate relevant newer state | Temporal weighting and supersession rules |
| Code/text disconnect | Policy and code drift apart | Cross-domain bridge relations and drift reports |
| CAS opacity | Human users cannot understand hash-based storage | Projection layer and stable human-facing labels |
| Schema creep | Ontology becomes unstable | Governance board or change-control process |

* * *

## 22. Launch Artifact Manifest

This section defines the foundational artifact inventory required for a solid launch. “Solid launch” here means durable, governable, and extensible, not merely demo-capable.

The following reduced set is the true minimum for a serious foundation.

| Phase | Output |
| --- | --- |
| Phase 1 | Governance pack and ontology pack |
| Phase 2 | Schema pack and storage decision pack |
| Phase 3 | Text refinery and code refinery specs |
| Phase 4 | GraphQL schema and retrieval spec |
| Phase 5 | Assembly/recipe spec and report formats |
| Phase 6 | Operational SOPs and evaluation harnesses |
| Phase 7 | Seed corpus and pilot validation |

* * *

## 25. Final Normative Conclusion

A valid v1 of this system MUST include:

Graph.  
Vector retrieval.  
Content-addressable storage.  
A preserved raw source archive.  
A typed GraphQL interface.  
`TextAtom` and `CodeAtom` as first-class types.  
Separate refineries for text and code.  
Shared governance, provenance, and recipe logic.  
Launch artifacts sufficient to operate, validate, and evolve the system.

Anything less than that may still be a useful prototype, but it is not yet a foundational atomic knowledge substrate in the full sense defined by this specification.

## 26. Immediate next drafting set

The highest-value next package is this five-document cluster:

| Next document | Purpose |
| --- | --- |
| Ontology Charter v1 | Freeze core types, classes, and relations |
| Schema Pack v1 | Formalize machine-readable schemas |
| Text Refinery Spec v1 | Define textual atomization pipeline |
| Code Refinery Spec v1 | Define AST-aware technical atomization |
| GraphQL Contract v1 | Define the system’s typed access surface |

Proceeding directly from here, the cleanest move is to draft the **Ontology Charter v1** in the same document-grade style.

## Q: 
I have two addendums from outside sources. What would be the best time to provide them to you?

## A: 
Now.

The best point to introduce external addenda is **before** the ontology charter and schema pack are drafted, because those two artifacts will lock vocabulary, object boundaries, and relation semantics. If the addenda materially affect atom classes, provenance rules, CAS assumptions, graph relations, code granularity, or interface design, bringing them in later creates avoidable churn.

Operationally, the best sequence is:

| Timing | Value |
| --- | --- |
| Before Ontology Charter v1 | Highest value; changes can still shape the conceptual model |
| Before Schema Pack v1 | Very high value; prevents schema rework |
| Before refinery specs | High value if the addenda affect atomization logic |
| After GraphQL contract | Much lower value; likely causes cascading revisions |

So the correct answer is: **provide them in the next message**.

If they are long, paste both in full and label them `ADDENDUM_A` and `ADDENDUM_B`. If they conflict with the current v1 spec, I will normalize them into one of three buckets:

| Bucket | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Accept | Should be integrated directly into v1 |
| Defer | Good idea, but better for v1.1+ |
| Reject / isolate | Conflicts with core architecture or introduces instability |

Then I will revise the architecture baseline accordingly before moving to the ontology charter.

## Q: 
Addendum Memorandum Subject: Architectural Evolution Plan for the Atomic Knowledge Assembler System Relation to Existing Repository: Conceptual Mapping and Expansion Status: Draft Purpose: Establish a forward architectural path that builds upon the existing system while avoiding duplication of implementation artifacts. ⸻ 1. Context The current repository represents a functioning knowledge ingestion, indexing, and retrieval environment capable of extracting value from conversations, documents, and external sources. Its capabilities include: FTS-based search vector similarity retrieval LLM-assisted extraction multi-source ingestion relationship inference web and CLI interfaces These elements already provide a practical knowledge extraction system. However, the architectural ambition has evolved toward something structurally stronger: an Atomic Knowledge Assembler, where knowledge exists as governed semantic primitives that can be recomposed into arbitrary outputs. The current repository should therefore be interpreted as Generation-1 infrastructure. This memorandum describes how to evolve it into Generation-2 architecture without discarding the functioning foundation. ⸻ 2. Architectural Shift The most important conceptual shift is: documents are no longer primary storage objects Instead: Atomic units become the persistent substrate. Documents become assembled projections. Generation-1 organizes knowledge around sources. Generation-2 organizes knowledge around semantic primitives. The goal is to transform the system from: Source → Index → Retrieve into: Source → Refinery → Atomic Graph → Assembly Engine ⸻ 3. Generation-1 Capabilities (Retained) The following subsystems from the current repository remain valid and should be retained. Ingestion Layer Existing multi-source ingestion is valuable and should remain. These include: conversation exports local files notes documents browser captures API-accessible content In Generation-2 this becomes the Source Intake Layer. The existing adapters can remain largely intact. ⸻ Hybrid Retrieval Stack The combination of lexical search and vector similarity is appropriate. Hybrid retrieval provides: precision via lexical matching semantic recall via embeddings This capability remains necessary in the future system. However, retrieval should operate on atoms, not on source fragments. ⸻ CLI and Web Interface The interface layers are also valuable. They provide: interactive exploration manual review capability debugging surfaces In Generation-2 these interfaces become assembly portals rather than simple search dashboards. ⸻ 4. Components Requiring Refactoring Several components must be structurally redesigned. ⸻ 4.1 Atom Definition The current atomic unit concept is primarily a searchable snippet. Generation-2 requires a stronger definition. An atom must be: self-contained contextually typed provenance-linked machine-addressable Atoms therefore become first-class semantic objects. Required Atom Classes The architecture should support multiple atom types. Examples include: TextAtom CodeAtom EvidenceAtom RelationAtom PolicyAtom RecipeAtom Each atom type represents a distinct functional role in reasoning. ⸻ 4.2 Immutable Identity Atoms require stable identifiers. Each atom must have: a permanent identifier a content fingerprint a provenance reference Content fingerprints allow the system to detect mutation and supersession. This introduces state mutation rather than version numbering. ⸻ 4.3 Provenance Precision Generation-1 provenance references sources at coarse levels. Generation-2 requires precise lineage. Each atom must track: origin artifact exact location within artifact transformation operations applied This enables auditing, verification, and error correction. ⸻ 4.4 Supersession Atomic systems require explicit change handling. Instead of overwriting existing data: old_atom → superseded_by → new_atom This allows the system to track knowledge evolution. ⸻ 4.5 Assembly Recipes Outputs must not be stored as static text artifacts. Instead the system stores assembly recipes. A recipe contains: ordered atom identifiers template instructions resolution level This enables outputs to regenerate automatically when atoms change. ⸻ 5. Refinery Pipeline Generation-2 introduces a formal knowledge refinery. The refinery converts raw sources into governed atoms. The pipeline consists of: source segmentation entity extraction proposition decomposition atomic distillation metadata crystallization deduplication validation The result is a set of semantic primitives suitable for recomposition. ⸻ 6. Code Corpus Integration The most significant expansion concerns code handling. The Generation-1 system treats code primarily as text fragments. Generation-2 must treat code as executable primitives. ⸻ 6.1 Code Atoms Code atoms represent functional units. Typical examples include: functions methods classes modules configuration blocks test cases Each code atom carries structured metadata such as: runtime language dependency references input/output signatures side-effect classification complexity indicators ⸻ 6.2 AST-Driven Refinement Code must be parsed structurally. Instead of regex extraction, the system should analyze: syntax trees symbol graphs dependency relationships This enables the system to understand intent rather than raw text. ⸻ 6.3 Dependency Graph Code atoms form dependency structures. These structures are represented as directed graphs. Dependency awareness enables: impact analysis automatic propagation of fixes cross-project bug awareness ⸻ 6.4 Cross-Domain Linking A key feature is text-to-code bridging. Examples include: policy atoms referencing enforcement logic documentation atoms referencing implementation atoms test atoms verifying code atoms This creates a unified knowledge-logic graph. ⸻ 7. Storage Architecture Evolution The storage model should expand into a hybrid system. The Generation-2 architecture contains four layers. Graph Substrate Stores relationships and dependency structures. Vector Substrate Stores embeddings for semantic retrieval. Source Archive Stores immutable raw artifacts. Content-Addressable Store Stores immutable atom payloads referenced by hash. ----- ADDENDUM 2 ----- Yes — design for it now That parallel linguistic-analysis system should not be treated as an external convenience. It should be treated as a first-class upstream producer in the overall architecture. If you do not design for it now, you will later end up with one of two bad outcomes: First, the linguistic system will dump opaque reports into the knowledge base as dead documents, which recreates the very monolith problem you are trying to escape. Second, you will over-couple the new knowledge base to the internal assumptions of the linguistic system, which will make both harder to evolve. The correct design is a federated atomic intake model: external analysis system produces structured findings → translation layer converts them into governed atoms → new knowledge base stores them as linked, typed, provenance-rich objects So the answer is yes: this absolutely needs to be designed for, and it should be designed as a formal integration lane, not an ad hoc import feature. ⸻ What it should look like conceptually You now have three distinct domains: Domain What it contains What it is good at Source domain raw conversations, documents, notes, code, media-derived text primary evidence Linguistic-analysis domain token patterns, syntax, rhetoric, discourse, semantic drift, ontology extraction, motif recurrence, style signatures interpretation and structural analysis Knowledge-base domain durable atoms, relations, recipes, provenance, assembly, cross-domain retrieval long-term governed memory The linguistic-analysis system should therefore be treated neither as raw evidence nor as final truth. It is a derivative analytical instrument. That means its outputs should enter the new system in a distinct ontological class, somewhere between evidence and interpretation. ⸻ The key design principle Do not import linguistic-analysis outputs as plain text reports. Instead, import them as structured analytical products that can be decomposed into atomic findings. The integration model should be: Raw source ↓ Parallel linguistic-analysis system ↓ Analytical export package ↓ Translation / normalization layer ↓ Knowledge atoms + relation atoms + provenance atoms + confidence metadata ↓ Assembly-ready knowledge substrate The crucial piece is the translation / normalization layer. That is the membrane between systems. Without that membrane, the knowledge base gets polluted with foreign assumptions, foreign schemas, and ungoverned interpretation objects. ⸻ What kinds of things the linguistic system would produce The external linguistic-analysis system may generate many classes of output. These should be anticipated now. A non-exhaustive analytical ontology would include the following families: Output family Example Lexical findings recurrent word clusters, terminology emergence, rare vocabulary spikes Syntactic findings sentence-complexity trends, clause chaining, imperative density Semantic findings concept neighborhoods, synonym drift, semantic compression, domain mapping Discourse findings topic transitions, framing shifts, narrative pivots, self-reference density Pragmatic findings intent patterns, directive vs exploratory tone, uncertainty markers Rhetorical findings metaphor patterns, contrast structures, repetition motifs, persuasive framing Ontological findings entity extraction, concept hierarchies, category proposals, taxonomy suggestions Temporal findings language drift over time, concept evolution, recurring sequences Comparative findings differences across projects, time windows, authors, systems, or modalities Signature findings stylistic fingerprints, preferred structures, recurrent symbolic patterns These outputs should not all be treated the same way. Some are more like evidence, some more like interpretation, some more like proposed ontology, and some more like diagnostics. So the knowledge base must distinguish them formally. ⸻ What new atom types you need To support this, I would extend the v2 ontology with a specific analysis lane. At minimum, add these atom classes: Atom type Purpose AnalysisAtom a normalized analytical finding ObservationAtom lower-level pattern directly observed from a corpus InterpretationAtom an inferential conclusion derived from observations MetricAtom numeric output from the linguistic system TaxonomyProposalAtom proposed category, cluster, or concept grouping SignatureAtom persistent stylistic or structural pattern DriftAtom a change-over-time pattern in language or meaning AnalysisRunAtom metadata about one execution of the external analysis pipeline These should be distinct from ordinary TextAtom, CodeAtom, and EvidenceAtom. That matters because a sentence in a source conversation and a sentence produced by a linguistic-analysis engine are not the same kind of object. One is source evidence. The other is analytical output about that source. ⸻ Provenance model for the parallel system This is where most systems fail. You need two-layer provenance at minimum, ideally three-layer provenance. Layer 1: source provenance What raw corpus was analyzed? For example: conversation IDs document IDs time windows author scopes project scopes code scopes selection filters Layer 2: analysis provenance What exact analytical run produced the result? For example: analysis engine name version prompt or model config algorithm class parameters dictionary / ontology versions timestamp confidence method Layer 3: transformation provenance How was the external result translated into the knowledge base? For example: normalization rules schema version import job ID conflict-resolution logic deduplication outcome This gives you traceability from final stored finding back to both the raw source and the analytical mechanism that produced it. Without this, analytical outputs become untrustworthy very quickly. ⸻ How the integration should work architecturally The cleanest model is a publish-normalize-ingest pattern. 1. Publish The linguistic-analysis system should export structured result bundles, not prose-only summaries. Those bundles should be machine-readable and stable. The export object should contain: run metadata corpus scope findings metrics links back to source spans confidence values proposed relations optional embeddings optional cluster identifiers 2. Normalize A dedicated integration service reads the export and maps it to the knowledge-base ontology. This service should: resolve source references convert external identifiers to internal identifiers separate observations from interpretations assign atom classes add validation state merge duplicates record provenance generate relation edges 3. Ingest The normalized output is stored as first-class atoms and linked into the broader graph. At this stage the system can connect: analysis findings to source evidence analysis findings to text atoms analysis findings to code atoms analysis findings to prior analyses analysis findings to recipes and assemblies ⸻ The data contract you should define now You need an explicit contract between the external linguistic system and the new knowledge base. This does not need to be technologically fancy at first, but it must be semantically strict. The external system should never “just send a paragraph.” It should send something like a structured analytical envelope with fields equivalent to: Field Meaning analysis_run_id unique ID for one run analysis_type discourse, semantic drift, syntax, rhetoric, etc. source_scope what corpus or slice was analyzed finding_id stable ID for each exported finding finding_kind observation, interpretation, metric, taxonomy proposal, signature finding_text normalized human-readable statement evidence_refs source spans or source atom IDs confidence numeric or categorical confidence method algorithm/model/process used timestamp when produced supersedes prior finding if applicable tags ontology or domain tags relations explicit suggested edges to internal objects That contract is what allows the two systems to evolve independently. ⸻ How to prevent contamination of the core knowledge base You do not want every analytical output immediately treated as stable truth. So you need a trust gradient. I recommend the following validation states for imported analysis objects: State Meaning imported accepted from external system, not yet reviewed machine-derived known to be analysis-generated reviewed checked by human or trusted adjudicator accepted allowed in normal assembly for standard outputs experimental visible only in exploratory or research contexts disputed challenged or contradicted deprecated superseded by newer or better analysis This keeps the analytical lane useful without letting it silently rewrite the ontology. ⸻ The most important relation types To make the parallel system genuinely useful, define these edge types from the start. Relation Meaning analyzes analysis object analyzes a source or atom derived_from finding comes from a source span or atom set supports finding strengthens another atom or interpretation contradicts finding conflicts with another atom or interpretation proposes_taxonomy_for analysis proposes ontology over a corpus detects_drift_in identifies change over time in an entity, topic, or style characterizes gives a structural description of an entity/corpus/project maps_to aligns an external analysis label to an internal concept requires_review_of flags atom or code object for re-evaluation is_superseded_by analysis result replaced by newer run These edges are what convert “interesting reports” into operational knowledge. ⸻ How this becomes practically useful Once integrated correctly, the linguistic-analysis system can do more than annotate language. It becomes a trigger system for knowledge maintenance. Examples: A semantic-drift finding can indicate that a concept has changed meaning across a project over six months, which should trigger taxonomy review. A rhetoric-pattern finding can reveal that a set of memos consistently mixes instruction and speculation, which should trigger atom reclassification. A business-rule language shift can be linked to code atoms implementing that rule, which should trigger impact analysis. A motif recurrence analysis can identify latent conceptual clusters across notes, which can seed new ontology branches. A discourse-structure analysis can produce reusable recipes for assembling future reports in the style that best matches the corpus. That is when the external analytical system stops being “another report generator” and becomes a genuine co-processor for the knowledge OS. ⸻ Whether this should be synchronous or asynchronous Architecturally, this should usually be asynchronous at the system level, even though conceptually it is parallel. The linguistic system should run on its own cadence and publish result bundles. The knowledge base should ingest those bundles through a controlled pipeline. That keeps the systems decoupled and resilient. However, the knowledge base should also support on-demand federation, meaning an assembly or query can ask: “show me source atoms plus the latest accepted linguistic analyses relevant to this topic” So the systems are operationally decoupled but logically composable. ⸻ Recommended structural pattern The cleanest pattern is this: Core substrate Stores source atoms, code atoms, evidence atoms, recipes, and accepted analysis atoms. External analysis exchange layer Receives export bundles from the linguistic-analysis system. Normalization membrane Maps foreign results into local ontology and trust states. Analytical graph lane Stores imported analysis runs and findings as a distinct subgraph. Assembly policy layer Determines when analytical findings are included in normal outputs, exploratory outputs, or deep-research outputs. That gives you a separation between memory, analysis, and rendering. ⸻ What I would explicitly design now I would design five things immediately. 1. A foreign-analysis import schema This is the contract for analytical result bundles. 2. New atom classes for derivative analysis Without these, the system will flatten evidence and interpretation together. 3. A provenance model for analysis runs You will need this sooner than you think. 4. A trust and validation policy So imported analysis does not silently become canon. 5. A relation vocabulary for cross-system linking This is what makes the integration operational instead of decorative. ⸻ My recommendation Yes, design for this now. But do not design it as “another source adapter.” Design it as a parallel analytical producer with a formal exchange contract and a protected ontology boundary. That is the right abstraction. In one line: the new knowledge base should ingest not just sources, but also governed interpretations of sources If you want, the next best step is for me to draft a v1 external-analysis integration spec with the exact object model for AnalysisRun, AnalysisFinding, relation edges, trust states, and import workflow. This layered approach balances: semantic search logical reasoning historical traceability ⸻ 8. Assembly Layer The assembly engine converts atoms into outputs. This process includes: scope determination atom selection structural arrangement connective synthesis The assembly layer allows the same knowledge to appear as: summaries technical documentation analysis reports decision memos ⸻ 9. Governance Layer Atomic knowledge systems require governance. Important governance functions include: validation states contradiction handling trust weighting policy enforcement Without governance the atomic pool becomes noisy. ⸻ 10. Migration Strategy The existing repository should evolve gradually. A recommended approach is parallel schema introduction. Generation-2 atoms can coexist with existing units. Migration steps include: introducing new atom schema adding a refinery pipeline gradually shifting retrieval to new atoms maintaining compatibility during transition This approach preserves operational functionality while evolving the system. ⸻ 11. Conceptual Model The final architecture may be summarized as: Sources ↓ Refinery ↓ Atomic Graph ↓ Assembly Engine ↓ Rendered Knowledge ⸻ 12. Strategic Outcome When complete, the system functions as a knowledge operating system. Knowledge becomes: composable traceable update-propagating cross-domain Documents, summaries, and analyses become temporary renderings of atomic truth. ⸻ 13. Next Recommended Step The next document should define the Generation-2 atom schema and identity model. This schema will determine: data structure refinery behavior storage design assembly semantics Because once atom identity is defined, the remainder of the system follows logically. ⸻ If useful, the next step could also include a visual architecture diagram showing the full refinery → atom pool → assembly pipeline, because that will make the system dramatically easier to reason about during development.

## A: 
# Addendum Integration Review

## Impact on UAKS-v1 Architecture Specification

The two addenda introduce **no contradictions to the core architecture**, but they **extend the ontology and pipeline design in three significant ways**:

1.  They formalize the **Generation-1 → Generation-2 migration path**.
    
2.  They introduce a **distinct analytical producer domain**.
    
3.  They require **additional atom classes and provenance layers**.
    

Both addenda are therefore **accepted with integration**, with minor structural adjustments so they remain compatible with the existing specification.

The outcome is an expanded architecture where **three knowledge production domains coexist** while preserving atomic governance.

* * *

# 1. Integration Decision

| Addendum | Decision | Reason |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Addendum Memorandum | **Accept** | Aligns with the architecture already defined |
| Linguistic Analysis Integration | **Accept with extension** | Requires additional atom families and provenance layers |

No element in the addenda conflicts with the core architectural principles.

They mainly clarify:

Generation-1 migration  
atomic schema expansion  
external analysis federation

* * *

# 2. Updated Domain Model

The architecture now explicitly recognizes **three production domains**.

| Domain | Function | Trust Level |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Source Domain | Raw evidence corpus | Highest |
| Analysis Domain | Derived analytical interpretations | Intermediate |
| Knowledge Substrate | Governed atomic knowledge | Canonical operational layer |

The **analysis domain is not evidence** and **not final truth**.

It is an **interpretive instrument** that feeds structured findings into the knowledge substrate.

* * *

# 3. Updated Architectural Topology

The system pipeline now becomes:

```
Sources   ↓Source Intake Layer   ↓Refinery   ↓Atomic Knowledge Substrate   ↓Assembly Engine   ↓Rendered Knowledge
```

With an additional **parallel analytical lane**:

```
Sources   ↓External Linguistic Analysis System   ↓Analytical Export Bundle   ↓Normalization Membrane   ↓Analysis Atoms + Relations   ↓Atomic Knowledge Substrate
```

Both pipelines ultimately feed the **same atomic graph**.

* * *

# 4. New Atom Families Introduced

The original architecture defined:

TextAtom  
CodeAtom  
EvidenceAtom  
RelationAtom  
PolicyAtom  
RecipeAtom

The addenda require a **distinct analytical ontology**.

### New analytical atom classes

| Atom Type | Purpose |
| --- | --- |
| AnalysisAtom | Generic normalized analytical finding |
| ObservationAtom | Directly observed pattern in corpus |
| InterpretationAtom | Analytical inference derived from observations |
| MetricAtom | Quantitative output from analysis pipeline |
| TaxonomyProposalAtom | Proposed ontology or classification |
| SignatureAtom | Persistent stylistic pattern |
| DriftAtom | Temporal semantic or linguistic shift |
| AnalysisRunAtom | Metadata for one analysis execution |

These atoms MUST remain **distinct from TextAtom and EvidenceAtom**.

* * *

# 5. Analytical Ontology Position

Analytical atoms occupy a **middle epistemic tier**.

```
Evidence   ↓Observation   ↓Interpretation   ↓Accepted Knowledge
```

Where:

| Tier | Atom Type |
| --- | --- |
| Evidence | EvidenceAtom |
| Observation | ObservationAtom |
| Interpretation | InterpretationAtom |
| Canonical Knowledge | TextAtom / CodeAtom |

* * *

# 6. Analytical Provenance Model

Addendum 2 introduces **three-layer provenance**.

The architecture specification is updated accordingly.

### Layer 1 — Source Provenance

Defines the raw corpus scope.

Example fields:

| Field | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| corpus_ids | Source documents analyzed |
| conversation_ids | Chat records |
| author_scope | Author or system scope |
| time_window | Temporal slice |

* * *

### Layer 2 — Analysis Provenance

Defines the analytical run itself.

| Field | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| analysis_engine | Tool or model name |
| version | Engine version |
| algorithm | Analytical method |
| parameters | Configuration |
| ontology_version | Vocabulary used |
| timestamp | Execution time |

* * *

### Layer 3 — Transformation Provenance

Defines how findings were normalized.

| Field | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| import_job_id | Import run |
| normalization_schema | Schema version |
| conflict_resolution | Merge rules |
| deduplication_result | Merge outcome |

* * *

# 7. Analytical Import Pipeline

The addenda introduce a **publish-normalize-ingest pattern**.

### Stage 1 — Publish

External analysis system produces structured bundles.

Required fields:

| Field | Description |
| --- | --- |
| analysis_run_id | Unique run identifier |
| analysis_type | Discourse / semantic / syntax / rhetoric |
| source_scope | Corpus selection |
| finding_id | Stable finding ID |
| finding_kind | Observation / interpretation / metric |
| finding_text | Normalized statement |
| evidence_refs | Source spans |
| confidence | Confidence score |
| method | Algorithm used |
| timestamp | Produced time |
| supersedes | Prior finding |
| tags | Ontology tags |
| relations | Proposed graph edges |

* * *

### Stage 2 — Normalize

A dedicated service performs translation.

Functions:

| Operation | Description |
| --- | --- |
| identifier mapping | Convert external IDs to internal IDs |
| schema conversion | Map external fields to atom schema |
| ontology mapping | Align external tags to internal ontology |
| trust assignment | Apply validation state |
| deduplication | Merge equivalent findings |
| relation generation | Create graph edges |
| provenance creation | Record transformation lineage |

* * *

### Stage 3 — Ingest

Normalized atoms enter the graph.

Possible links:

| Link | Target |
| --- | --- |
| analysis → source | Raw source spans |
| analysis → text atom | Claims analyzed |
| analysis → code atom | Implementation referenced |
| analysis → analysis | Temporal comparison |
| analysis → entity | Concept classification |

* * *

# 8. Trust Gradient for Analytical Atoms

Analytical outputs must not automatically become canonical.

New validation states are introduced.

| State | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| imported | Raw analytical import |
| machine_derived | Automatically generated analysis |
| reviewed | Human validation |
| accepted | Allowed in standard assemblies |
| experimental | Restricted to research outputs |
| disputed | Challenged finding |
| deprecated | Superseded analysis |

* * *

# 9. New Relation Vocabulary

Addendum 2 introduces additional graph relations.

| Relation | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| analyzes | Analytical object studies a corpus |
| derived_from | Finding derived from source |
| supports | Analytical evidence supports claim |
| contradicts | Analytical result conflicts with atom |
| proposes_taxonomy_for | Suggests ontology structure |
| detects_drift_in | Identifies temporal change |
| characterizes | Structural description of corpus |
| maps_to | Aligns external concept to internal entity |
| requires_review_of | Flags atom for review |
| is_superseded_by | Analytical finding replaced |

* * *

# 10. Migration Strategy Update

Addendum 1 describes **Generation-1 → Generation-2 transition**.

The architecture now formally supports **parallel schema coexistence**.

### Migration steps

| Step | Action |
| --- | --- |
| 1 | Introduce Generation-2 atom schema |
| 2 | Implement refinery pipeline |
| 3 | Store atoms alongside existing repository objects |
| 4 | Shift retrieval gradually to atom graph |
| 5 | Maintain compatibility during transition |
| 6 | Retire legacy indexing structures |

This allows gradual transformation.

* * *

# 11. Updated Storage Model

The hybrid storage architecture remains unchanged but gains an **analytical lane**.

```
               Raw Source Archive                      │                      ▼                Source Intake                      │            ┌─────────┴─────────┐            ▼                   ▼      Text Refinery       Code Refinery            │                   │            └───────┬───────────┘                    ▼              Atomic Graph                    │       ┌────────────┴────────────┐       ▼                         ▼   Vector Index            CAS Storage       │                         │       └────────────┬────────────┘                    ▼             Assembly Engine                    │                    ▼           Rendered Knowledge
```

Parallel analytical lane:

```
External Linguistic System            │            ▼      Export Bundle            │            ▼    Normalization Layer            │            ▼      Analysis Atom Graph            │            ▼      Atomic Knowledge Graph
```

* * *

# 12. Updated Atom Hierarchy

The complete atom hierarchy now becomes:

```
Atom ├── TextAtom ├── CodeAtom ├── EvidenceAtom ├── RelationAtom ├── PolicyAtom ├── RecipeAtom │ └── AnalysisAtoms      ├── AnalysisAtom      ├── ObservationAtom      ├── InterpretationAtom      ├── MetricAtom      ├── TaxonomyProposalAtom      ├── SignatureAtom      ├── DriftAtom      └── AnalysisRunAtom
```

* * *

# 13. Operational Implications

With these addenda integrated, the system becomes capable of:

| Capability | Description |
| --- | --- |
| semantic drift detection | track concept evolution |
| ontology suggestion | propose new concept hierarchies |
| discourse analysis | detect narrative structure patterns |
| policy-code drift detection | detect divergence between rules and implementation |
| stylistic fingerprinting | identify recurring patterns |
| automated ontology maintenance | flag categories needing revision |

* * *

# 14. Updated Strategic Outcome

The resulting architecture becomes:

```
Evidence system+Analysis system+Knowledge substrate=Knowledge operating system
```

The system therefore supports:

composable knowledge  
traceable interpretation  
update propagation  
cross-domain reasoning  
analysis-assisted ontology evolution

* * *

# 15. Final Architectural Status

| Component | Status |
| --- | --- |
| Generation-1 migration plan | Accepted |
| Atomic schema expansion | Accepted |
| Analytical integration lane | Accepted |
| Hybrid storage architecture | Confirmed |
| External analysis contract | Required |

* * *

# 16. Immediate Next Document

With the addenda integrated, the **correct next artifact** is:

**Ontology Charter v1**

This document will freeze:

Atom families  
Relation vocabulary  
Entity classes  
Validation states  
Trust model

Once that charter exists, the rest of the system becomes straightforward to implement.

**2\. The Ontology Charter v1 document**

The **Ontology Charter** should come first because it locks the vocabulary for everything else.

# 2. Ontology Charter v1

## Unified Atomic Knowledge Substrate

**Document ID:** `uaks_v1_ontology_charter_20260311`  
**Version:** `1.0-draft`  
**Status:** Draft normative charter

## 2.1 Purpose

This charter defines the canonical ontology for UAKS-v1. It establishes the first-class object families, the relation vocabulary, the trust model, and the boundary between evidence, interpretation, executable logic, and derivative analysis.

## 2.2 Ontological Thesis

The system MUST distinguish between:

| Layer | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Source evidence | What existed in the raw corpus |
| Atomic knowledge | Governed, typed, reusable units extracted from or derived from sources |
| Derivative analysis | Structured findings produced by analytical systems about sources or atoms |
| Assemblies | Temporary or persisted renderings composed from atoms |

A raw sentence in a source artifact is not ontologically identical to a normalized rule atom. A normalized rule atom is not ontologically identical to an analytical observation about rhetorical drift. These objects MAY be linked, but they MUST NOT be flattened into a single undifferentiated text object.

## 2.3 Core Object Families

| Object Family | Role | First-Class |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Atom | Abstract root type for atomic objects | Yes |
| TextAtom | Atomic textual meaning | Yes |
| CodeAtom | Atomic executable or technical logic | Yes |
| EvidenceAtom | Source-backed support or extracted datum | Yes |
| PolicyAtom | Normative rule or constraint | Yes |
| RelationAtom | Reified relation when relation itself needs metadata | Yes |
| RecipeAtom | Assembly plan as atomic object | Yes |
| AnalysisAtom | Normalized analytical finding | Yes |
| ObservationAtom | Direct analytical observation | Yes |
| InterpretationAtom | Inferential analytical conclusion | Yes |
| MetricAtom | Quantitative analytical output | Yes |
| TaxonomyProposalAtom | Proposed ontology/classification object | Yes |
| SignatureAtom | Persistent stylistic or structural pattern | Yes |
| DriftAtom | Temporal semantic/stylistic change pattern | Yes |
| AnalysisRunAtom | One analysis execution record | Yes |
| Entity | Referenced domain object | Yes |
| SourceObject | Registered source artifact | Yes |
| ProvenanceRecord | Lineage and transformation object | Yes |

## 2.4 Root Atom Contract

All atom types inherit the same root obligations.

| Constraint ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| OC-ATOM-01 | Every atom MUST have a stable logical identifier. |
| OC-ATOM-02 | Every atom MUST have a content fingerprint or equivalent immutable state identity. |
| OC-ATOM-03 | Every atom MUST have a declared type and class. |
| OC-ATOM-04 | Every verified atom MUST have provenance. |
| OC-ATOM-05 | Every atom SHOULD be independently interpretable within subtype rules. |
| OC-ATOM-06 | Atoms MAY be superseded but MUST NOT be silently overwritten once verified. |

## 2.5 Atom Families

### 2.5.1 TextAtom

A `TextAtom` is the smallest governed unit of textual meaning that can stand alone without hidden local context.

Typical uses include requirements, documentation clauses, notes, claims, normalized statements, and descriptive assertions.

### 2.5.2 CodeAtom

A `CodeAtom` is the smallest governed unit of executable or technical logic suitable for dependency reasoning, traceability, impact analysis, and reassembly.

`CodeAtom` categories MUST include at least:

| Code Kind |
| --- |
| FUNCTION |
| METHOD |
| CLASS |
| MODULE |
| CONFIG |
| QUERY |
| SCRIPT_STEP |
| TEST_CASE |
| SCHEMA_UNIT |
| UI_COMPONENT |
| INFRA_UNIT |

### 2.5.3 EvidenceAtom

An `EvidenceAtom` is a source-backed support unit. It anchors claims, observations, or interpretations to extractable evidence.

Examples include measured values, cited statements, source fragments, or exact spans needed for verification.

### 2.5.4 PolicyAtom

A `PolicyAtom` is a normative unit expressing what SHOULD, MUST, MAY, MUST NOT, or SHOULD NOT happen in an operational, legal, procedural, or governance context.

### 2.5.5 RelationAtom

A `RelationAtom` is used when a relation itself requires additional metadata, provenance, confidence, time scope, or adjudication.

### 2.5.6 RecipeAtom

A `RecipeAtom` represents an assembly pattern that can regenerate outputs from ordered atom sets plus template and resolution rules.

### 2.5.7 Analysis Family

The analytical lane is a first-class derivative domain.

| Type | Purpose |
| --- | --- |
| AnalysisAtom | General normalized analytical finding |
| ObservationAtom | Pattern directly observed from corpus or atom set |
| InterpretationAtom | Inferential conclusion derived from observations |
| MetricAtom | Numeric or scored output |
| TaxonomyProposalAtom | Suggested ontology or grouping |
| SignatureAtom | Stable stylistic pattern |
| DriftAtom | Temporal change pattern |
| AnalysisRunAtom | Metadata for a single analytical execution |

## 2.6 Epistemic Tiers

The ontology MUST preserve epistemic distinctions.

| Tier | Canonical Types | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Tier 1 | SourceObject | Raw evidence-bearing artifacts |
| Tier 2 | EvidenceAtom, TextAtom, CodeAtom, PolicyAtom | Governed primary substrate |
| Tier 3 | ObservationAtom, InterpretationAtom, MetricAtom, DriftAtom, SignatureAtom, TaxonomyProposalAtom | Derivative analysis over sources or atoms |
| Tier 4 | RecipeAtom, Assemblies | Rendered or reusable composition layer |

This means analytical outputs are neither raw evidence nor equivalent to source-grounded rules by default.

## 2.7 Entity Ontology

Entities are not atoms. They are referenced domain objects.

A minimum v1 entity lattice SHOULD include:

| Entity Class | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| Person | Human actor |
| Organization | Group, institution, company, team |
| Project | Named work program |
| Repository | Technical codebase or knowledge repository |
| Module | Technical subsystem |
| Service | Runtime or system service |
| Interface | Contract surface |
| PolicyDomain | Normative domain |
| Concept | Abstract idea |
| Term | Canonical lexical item |
| Topic | Thematic grouping |
| Dataset | Structured data object |
| Artifact | General produced object |
| Environment | Runtime or deployment context |
| TimeWindow | Temporal scope object |

## 2.8 Relation Vocabulary

The relation vocabulary is canonical. Additional relations MAY be added in later versions, but the following set is normative for v1.

### 2.8.1 Core Relations

| Relation | Source | Target | Meaning |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| DERIVED_FROM | Atom | SourceObject or Atom | Origin linkage |
| SUPPORTED_BY | Atom | EvidenceAtom or Atom | Support relation |
| CONTRADICTS | Atom | Atom | Conflict relation |
| SUPERSEDES | Atom | Atom | Successor relation |
| USES_ENTITY | Atom | Entity | Entity reference |
| ASSEMBLED_IN | Atom | RecipeAtom | Recipe membership |
| REFINES | Atom | Atom | More precise or granular version |

### 2.8.2 Text-Code Bridge Relations

| Relation | Source | Target | Meaning |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IMPLEMENTS | CodeAtom | TextAtom or PolicyAtom | Code realizes textual rule |
| DOCUMENTS | TextAtom | CodeAtom | Text describes code |
| TESTS | CodeAtom or TestAtom-like CodeAtom | CodeAtom | Validation of technical logic |
| AFFECTS | PolicyAtom or TextAtom | CodeAtom | Rule impacts code behavior |
| EXPOSES_INTERFACE | CodeAtom | Entity | Code provides interface |

### 2.8.3 Analysis Relations

| Relation | Source | Target | Meaning |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ANALYZES | AnalysisAtom family | SourceObject or Atom | Analytical object studies target |
| MAPS_TO | AnalysisAtom family | Entity or Atom | External label aligned to internal concept |
| CHARACTERIZES | AnalysisAtom family | Entity, Project, Corpus | Structural description |
| DETECTS_DRIFT_IN | DriftAtom | Entity or Atom | Change-over-time finding |
| PROPOSES_TAXONOMY_FOR | TaxonomyProposalAtom | Entity, corpus, concept set | Ontology suggestion |
| REQUIRES_REVIEW_OF | AnalysisAtom family | Atom | Trigger re-evaluation |
| IS_SUPERSEDED_BY | AnalysisAtom family | AnalysisAtom family | Analytical successor |

## 2.9 Validation and Trust States

The system has a general lifecycle, and analytical imports have an extended trust gradient.

### 2.9.1 Core Validation States

| State | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| DRAFT | Not yet checked |
| DISTILLED | Machine-generated and schema-valid |
| REVIEWED | Human or trusted review performed |
| VERIFIED | Approved for normal assembly |
| DEPRECATED | Retained but not active |
| DISPUTED | Challenged |

### 2.9.2 Analysis Import Trust States

| State | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| IMPORTED | Received from external analytical producer |
| MACHINE_DERIVED | Known analysis-generated object |
| REVIEWED | Checked by human or trusted adjudicator |
| ACCEPTED | Allowed in standard assemblies |
| EXPERIMENTAL | Restricted to research/exploratory contexts |
| DISPUTED | Challenged |
| DEPRECATED | Superseded or retired |

## 2.10 Provenance Ontology

The ontology adopts a three-layer provenance model for derivative analytical outputs and a two-layer minimum for all other atoms.

| Provenance Layer | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| Source provenance | MUST identify original corpus or artifact scope |
| Analysis provenance | MUST exist for analytical lane objects |
| Transformation provenance | MUST record normalization/import/refinery actions |

## 2.11 Supersession Semantics

Supersession is a first-class ontological rule.

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| OC-SUP-01 | Knowledge evolution MUST be modeled with explicit successor relations. |
| OC-SUP-02 | A new payload state MUST produce a new content identity. |
| OC-SUP-03 | Supersession chains SHOULD remain acyclic under normal operation. |

## 2.12 Resolution Model

The ontology supports multi-scale assembly.

| Resolution | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| MICRO | Minimal core claim or logic unit |
| COMPACT | Essential support only |
| STANDARD | Balanced explanation |
| EXTENDED | Detailed exposition |
| DEEP | Evidence-rich and contradiction-aware |

## 2.13 Ontology Change Policy

| Rule ID | Requirement |
| --- | --- |
| OC-CHG-01 | New atom families MAY be introduced only through ontology revision control. |
| OC-CHG-02 | Existing first-class types MUST NOT be merged casually. |
| OC-CHG-03 | Cross-domain distinctions between evidence, primary atoms, and analytical atoms MUST be preserved. |

## 2.14 Final Charter Judgment

The v1 ontology is therefore a **tripartite substrate**:

| Domain | Ontological Role |
| --- | --- |
| Source domain | Evidence-bearing raw reality |
| Primary atomic domain | Governed knowledge and technical logic |
| Analytical derivative domain | Structured interpretation and diagnostics |

That tripartite distinction is now canonical.

* * *

# 3. GraphQL Schema Draft v1

## Unified Atomic Knowledge Substrate API Contract

Below is a document-grade draft schema. It is intentionally concrete enough to implement, but still conservative enough to revise without breaking the ontology.
